</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Mathematical-logic system based on functions</div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:LambdaAbstraction.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/LambdaAbstraction.svg/250px-LambdaAbstraction.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/LambdaAbstraction.svg/500px-LambdaAbstraction.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="614" data-file-height="304" /></a><figcaption>The lambda abstraction decomposed. The <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b43d0ea3c9c025af1be9128e62a18fa74bedda2a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.355ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda }"></span> indicates the start of a function. <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x}"></span> is the input parameter. <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle M}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>M</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle M}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f82cade9898ced02fdd08712e5f0c0151758a0dd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.442ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle M}"></span> is the body, separated by a dot separator "<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle .}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle .}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1e44e5c7036d244e546db1167ed820d947fcd63a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.647ex; height:0.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle .}"></span>" from the input parameter.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_logic" title="Mathematical logic">mathematical logic</a>, the <b>lambda calculus</b> (also written as <b><i>λ</i>-calculus</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Formal_system" title="Formal system">formal system</a> for expressing <a href="/wiki/Computability" title="Computability">computation</a> based on function <a href="/wiki/Abstraction_(computer_science)" title="Abstraction (computer science)">abstraction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Function_application" title="Function application">application</a> using variable <a href="/wiki/Name_binding" title="Name binding">binding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Substitution_(algebra)" class="mw-redirect" title="Substitution (algebra)">substitution</a>. Untyped lambda calculus, the topic of this article, is a <a href="/wiki/Universal_machine" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal machine">universal machine</a>, i.e. a <a href="/wiki/Model_of_computation" title="Model of computation">model of computation</a> that can be used to simulate any <a href="/wiki/Turing_machine" title="Turing machine">Turing machine</a> (and vice versa). It was introduced by the mathematician <a href="/wiki/Alonzo_Church" title="Alonzo Church">Alonzo Church</a> in the 1930s as part of his research into the <a href="/wiki/Foundations_of_mathematics" title="Foundations of mathematics">foundations of mathematics</a>. In 1936, Church found a formulation which was <a href="#History">logically consistent</a>, and documented it in 1940.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Definition">Definition</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lambda_calculus_definition" title="Lambda calculus definition">Lambda calculus definition</a></div>
<p>The lambda calculus consists of a language of <b>lambda terms</b>, which are defined by a formal syntax, and a set of transformation rules for manipulating those terms. In <a href="/wiki/Backus%E2%80%93Naur_form" title="Backus–Naur form">BNF</a>, the syntax is <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle e::=x\mid \lambda x.e\mid e\,e,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>e</mi>
        <mo>::=</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>&#x2223;<!-- ∣ --></mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>e</mi>
        <mo>&#x2223;<!-- ∣ --></mo>
        <mi>e</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>e</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e::=x\mid \lambda x.e\mid e\,e,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bd3e8f08ad9d74465759278a3203fc213c9c71e0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.683ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e::=x\mid \lambda x.e\mid e\,e,}"></span> where variables <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i>,<i>y</i>,<i>z</i></span> range over an infinite set of names. Terms <span class="texhtml"><i>M</i>,<i>N</i>,<i>t</i>,<i>s</i>,<i>e</i>,<i>f</i></span> range over all lambda terms. This corresponds to the following <a href="/wiki/Inductive_definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Inductive definition">inductive definition</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="anchor" id="validLambdaVar"></span> A <i>variable</i> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is a valid lambda term.</li>
<li><span class="anchor" id="lambdaAbstr"></span> An <i>abstraction</i> is a lambda term <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.t)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>t</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (\lambda x.t)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3579b47df6ceca7844a6718b01aea766d97f4e91" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.368ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.t)}"></span> where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">t</span> is a lambda term, referred to as the abstraction's <i>body</i>, and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is the abstraction's <i>parameter</i> variable,</li>
<li><span class="anchor" id="anApplic"></span> An <i>application</i> is a lambda term <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (t\,s)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>t</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>s</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (t\,s)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7775eec0095f546da907cd682b0c451e3431fde1" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.126ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (t\,s)}"></span> where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">t</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">s</span> are lambda terms.</li></ul>
<p>A lambda term is syntactically valid if it can be obtained by repeated application of these three rules. For convenience, parentheses can often be omitted when writing a lambda term—see <a href="/wiki/Lambda_calculus_definition#Notation" title="Lambda calculus definition">Lambda calculus definition §&#160;Notation</a> for details.
</p><p>Within lambda terms, any occurrence of a variable that is not a parameter of some enclosing λ is said to be <i>free</i>. Any free occurrence of <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x}"></span> in a term <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle M}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>M</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle M}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f82cade9898ced02fdd08712e5f0c0151758a0dd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.442ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle M}"></span> is <i>bound</i> in <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>M</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4c9948a242f678c85384a3547883313f99fe3324" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.161ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}"></span>. Any free occurrence of any other variable within <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle M}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>M</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle M}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f82cade9898ced02fdd08712e5f0c0151758a0dd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.442ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle M}"></span> remains free in <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>M</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4c9948a242f678c85384a3547883313f99fe3324" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.161ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}"></span>.  
</p><p>For example, in the term <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x\,y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\,y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/96ba0995888b0c84e81761ea534c3ae27cac5633" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.872ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x\,y}"></span>, both <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x}"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle y}"></span> occur free. In <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.x\,y)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da556b2d5ea3fc74bc692c250c573fb7013968a7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.4ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.x\,y)}"></span>, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle y}">
  <semantics>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle y}"></span> is free, but <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x}"></span> in the body (i.e. after the dot) is not free, and is said to be <i>bound</i> (to the parameter). While <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle y}"></span> is free in <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.x\,y)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>y</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (\lambda x.x\,y)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da556b2d5ea3fc74bc692c250c573fb7013968a7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.4ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.x\,y)}"></span>, it is bound in <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda y.\lambda x.x\,y)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>y</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>y</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (\lambda y.\lambda x.x\,y)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/571e40c026b57b9af5189475a8f2156e778aaade" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.945ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (\lambda y.\lambda x.x\,y)}"></span>. There are two occurrences of <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">

        <mi>x</mi>

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x}"></span> in <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda y.(\lambda x.x\,y)\,x)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/85afef6e16e55fa90f29812c34f8a61f7f881790" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.471ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (\lambda y.(\lambda x.x\,y)\,x)}"></span> – one is bound, and the other is free. 
</p><p><span class="texhtml">FV(M)</span> is the set of free variables of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">M</span>, i.e. such variables that occur free in <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">M</span> at least once. It can be defined inductively as follows:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \operatorname {FV} (x)=\{x\}}">
  <semantics>

        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \operatorname {FV} (x)=\{x\}}</annotation>
  </semantics>

<p>The notation <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle M[x:=N]}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2903f0b1ec544a7beb9cdca4dd72aed0e81e3494" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.874ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle M[x:=N]}"></span> denotes <b>capture-avoiding substitution</b>: substituting <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">N</span> for every free occurrence of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> in <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">M</span>, while avoiding variable capture.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This operation is defined inductively as follows:

<p>There are several notions of "equivalence" and "reduction" that make it possible to reduce lambda terms to equivalent lambda terms.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>α-conversion</i> captures the intuition that the particular choice of a bound variable, in an abstraction, does not (usually) matter. If <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle y\notin FV(M)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>y</mi>
        <mo>&#x2209;<!-- ∉ --></mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mi>V</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>M</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y\notin FV(M)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/85a1c82c5ae84b51df5b3dbbb484821436b6c7af" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.776ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle y\notin FV(M)}"></span>, then the terms <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>M</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4c9948a242f678c85384a3547883313f99fe3324" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.161ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.M}"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda y.M[x:=y]}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

        <mi>y</mi>

        <mi>M</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>:=</mo>
        <mi>y</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">]</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda y.M[x:=y]}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0534b41ca34589e48c25b7620eacc0036a83c70c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.511ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda y.M[x:=y]}"></span> are considered <i>alpha-equivalent</i>, written <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.M\equiv _{\alpha }\lambda y.M[x:=y]}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>M</mi>
        <msub>
          <mo>&#x2261;<!-- ≡ --></mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>&#x03B1;<!-- α --></mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>y</mi>

The equivalence relation is the smallest congruence relation on lambda terms generated by this rule. For instance, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.x}">

<li>The <i>β-reduction</i> rule states that a β-redex, an application of the form <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.t)s}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>t</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mi>s</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (\lambda x.t)s}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/56eb16cb15bc2d59d009c0b86ecd37e9ce6f7991" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:7.458ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.t)s}"></span>, reduces to the term <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle t[x:=s]}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>t</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>:=</mo>
        <mi>s</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">]</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle t[x:=s]}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c69396d99d4f60dbe54641cf62b9864b0a2251e1" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.299ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle t[x:=s]}"></span>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-beta&#95;5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beta-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>b<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, for every <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle s}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>s</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle s}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/01d131dfd7673938b947072a13a9744fe997e632" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle s}"></span>, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.x)s\to x[x:=s]=s}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mi>s</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>:=</mo>

        <mi>s</mi>

This demonstrates that <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.x}">
  <semantics>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/537ec33b43915b93dec1c98e433ec7a68bcab6a3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.049ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.x}"></span> really is the identity. Similarly, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda x.y)s\to y[x:=s]=y}">

        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda x.y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/88b2e10a12e276198f384ca3f5da934bdfaedc07" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.874ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.y}"></span> is a constant function.</li>
<li><i>η-conversion</i> expresses extensionality and converts between <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.fx}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda x.fx}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/21b3824f5895d6b57704d1bd2a852edce5d6bdd6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.327ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.fx}"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle f}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>f</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle f}"></span> whenever <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x}"></span> does not appear free in <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle f}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>f</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle f}"></span>. It is often omitted in many treatments of lambda calculus.</li></ul>
<p><span class="anchor" id="redex"></span>The term <i>redex</i>, short for <i>reducible expression</i>, refers to subterms that can be reduced by one of the reduction rules. For example, (λ<i>x</i>.<i>M</i>) <i>N</i> is a β-redex in expressing the substitution of <i>N</i> for <i>x</i> in <i>M</i>. The expression to which a redex reduces is called its <i>reduct</i>; the reduct of (λ<i>x</i>.<i>M</i>) <i>N</i> is <i>M</i>[<i>x</i>&#160;:= <i>N</i>].
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Explanation_and_applications">Explanation and applications</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Explanation and applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Lambda calculus is <a href="/wiki/Turing_completeness" title="Turing completeness">Turing complete</a>, that is, it is a universal <a href="/wiki/Model_of_computation" title="Model of computation">model of computation</a> that can be used to simulate any <a href="/wiki/Turing_machine" title="Turing machine">Turing machine</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its namesake, the Greek letter lambda (λ), is used in lambda expressions and lambda terms to denote <a href="/wiki/Free_variables_and_bound_variables" title="Free variables and bound variables">binding</a> a variable in a <a href="/wiki/Function_(mathematics)" title="Function (mathematics)">function</a>.
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="untyped&#95;lambda&#95;calculus"></span><span class="anchor" id="untypedLambdaCalculus"></span>Lambda calculus may be <i>untyped</i> or <i>typed</i>. In typed lambda calculus, functions can be applied only if they are capable of accepting the given input's "type" of data. Typed lambda calculi are strictly <i>weaker</i> than the untyped lambda calculus, which is the primary subject of this article, in the sense that <i>typed lambda calculi can express less</i> than the untyped calculus can. On the other hand, more things can be proven with typed lambda calculi. For example, in <a href="/wiki/Simply_typed_lambda_calculus" title="Simply typed lambda calculus">simply typed lambda calculus</a>, it is a theorem that every evaluation strategy terminates for every simply typed lambda-term,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Tait&#95;1967&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tait_1967-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> whereas evaluation of untyped lambda-terms need not terminate (see <a href="#betaReducIsAcomput">below</a>). One reason there are many different typed lambda calculi has been the desire to do more (of what the untyped calculus can do) without giving up on being able to prove strong theorems about the calculus.
</p><p>Lambda calculus has applications in many different areas in <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistics</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Lambda calculus has played an important role in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Programming_language_theory" title="Programming language theory">theory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming languages</a>. <a href="/wiki/Functional_programming" title="Functional programming">Functional programming</a> languages implement lambda calculus. Lambda calculus is also a current research topic in <a href="/wiki/Category_theory" title="Category theory">category theory</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2026)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Lambda calculus was introduced by mathematician <a href="/wiki/Alonzo_Church" title="Alonzo Church">Alonzo Church</a> in the 1930s as part of an investigation into the <a href="/wiki/Foundations_of_mathematics" title="Foundations of mathematics">foundations of mathematics</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>c<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The original system was shown to be <a href="/wiki/Consistency" title="Consistency">logically inconsistent</a> in 1935 when <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Kleene" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Kleene">Stephen Kleene</a> and <a href="/wiki/J._B._Rosser" class="mw-redirect" title="J. B. Rosser">J. B. Rosser</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/Kleene%E2%80%93Rosser_paradox" title="Kleene–Rosser paradox">Kleene–Rosser paradox</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Subsequently, in 1936 Church isolated and published just the portion relevant to computation, what is now called the untyped lambda calculus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Church1936&#95;18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Church1936-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1940, he also introduced a computationally weaker, but logically consistent system, known as the <a href="/wiki/Simply_typed_lambda_calculus" title="Simply typed lambda calculus">simply typed lambda calculus</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Until the 1960s when its relation to programming languages was clarified, the lambda calculus was only a formalism. Thanks to <a href="/wiki/Richard_Montague" title="Richard Montague">Richard Montague</a> and other linguists' applications in the semantics of natural language, the lambda calculus has begun to enjoy a respectable place in both linguistics<sup id="cite&#95;ref-mm-linguistics&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mm-linguistics-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and computer science.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Origin_of_the_λ_symbol"><span id="Origin_of_the_.CE.BB_symbol"></span>Origin of the <i>λ</i> symbol</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Origin of the λ symbol"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Origin&#95;of&#95;the&#95;lambda&#95;symbol"></span>
There is some uncertainty over the reason for Church's use of the Greek letter <a href="/wiki/Lambda" title="Lambda">lambda</a> (λ) as the notation for function-abstraction in the lambda calculus, perhaps in part due to conflicting explanations by Church himself. According to Cardone and Hindley (2006):
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>By the way, why did Church choose the notation "λ"? In [an unpublished 1964 letter to Harald Dickson] he stated clearly that it came from the notation "<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {x}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mover>
              <mi>x</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">&#x005E;<!-- ^ --></mo>
            </mover>
          </mrow>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {x}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18d95a7845e4e16ffb7e18ab37a208d0ab18e0e0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\hat {x}}}"></span>" used for class-abstraction by <a href="/wiki/Principia_Mathematica" title="Principia Mathematica">Whitehead and Russell</a>, by first modifying "<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {x}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

          </mrow>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {x}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18d95a7845e4e16ffb7e18ab37a208d0ab18e0e0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\hat {x}}}"></span>" to "<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \land x}">

</p><p>This origin was also reported in [Rosser, 1984, p.338]. On the other hand, in his later years Church told two enquirers that the choice was more accidental: a symbol was needed and λ just happened to be chosen.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dana_Scott" title="Dana Scott">Dana Scott</a> has also addressed this question in various public lectures.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
Scott recounts that he once posed a question about the origin of the lambda symbol to Church's former student and son-in-law John W. Addison Jr., who then wrote his father-in-law a postcard:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Dear Professor Church,
</p><p>Russell had the <a href="/wiki/Iota_operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Iota operator">iota operator</a>, Hilbert had the <a href="/wiki/Epsilon_operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Epsilon operator">epsilon operator</a>. Why did you choose lambda for your operator?
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>According to Scott, Church's entire response consisted of returning the postcard with the following annotation: "<a href="/wiki/Eeny,_meeny,_miny,_moe" title="Eeny, meeny, miny, moe">eeny, meeny, miny, moe</a>".
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Motivation">Motivation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Motivation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Computable_function" title="Computable function">Computable functions</a> are a fundamental concept within computer science and mathematics. The lambda calculus provides simple <a href="/wiki/Semantics#Computer_science" title="Semantics">semantics</a> for computation which are useful for formally studying properties of computation. The lambda calculus incorporates two simplifications that make its semantics simple.
<span class="anchor" id="anonymousForm"></span>The first simplification is that the lambda calculus treats functions "anonymously"; it does not give them explicit names. For example, the function
</p>

<p>can be rewritten in anonymous form as
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto x}">

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\mapsto x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/033c0ae81eaf4c65cbb0759d7aa2c4f434c00f02" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.273ex; height:1.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x\mapsto x}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>where the input is simply mapped to itself.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-mapsTo&#95;23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mapsTo-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>d<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The second simplification is that the lambda calculus only uses functions of a single input. An ordinary function that requires two inputs, for instance the <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle \operatorname {square\_sum} }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OP MJX-fixedlimits">
          <mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">q</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">u</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x005F;<!-- _ --></mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">u</mi>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\textstyle \operatorname {square\_sum} }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b1452ce7cbdc7fd26d4b880eddf9b28d0c4965a7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.866ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\textstyle \operatorname {square\_sum} }"></span> function, can be reworked into an equivalent function that accepts a single input, and as output returns <i>another</i> function, that in turn accepts a single input. For example,
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (x,y)\mapsto x^{2}+y^{2}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

        <mi>x</mi>

        <mi>y</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x21A6;<!-- ↦ --></mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>+</mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (x,y)\mapsto x^{2}+y^{2}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/89bf7c479bc1935d1ddd0519cde149591d0e541b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:16.382ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (x,y)\mapsto x^{2}+y^{2}}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>can be reworked into
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto (y\mapsto x^{2}+y^{2})}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x21A6;<!-- ↦ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>y</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x21A6;<!-- ↦ --></mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>+</mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\mapsto (y\mapsto x^{2}+y^{2})}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/012fc8f19ed14bf232ee8deefe4ae84dc507875d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.962ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x\mapsto (y\mapsto x^{2}+y^{2})}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>This method, known as <a href="/wiki/Currying" title="Currying">currying</a>, transforms a function that takes multiple arguments into a chain of functions each with a single argument.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Function_application" title="Function application">Function application</a> of the <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle \operatorname {square\_sum} }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

      </mstyle>

  </semantics>
