<p>to arrive at the same result.
</p><p>In lambda calculus, functions are taken to be '<a href="/wiki/First-class_object" class="mw-redirect" title="First-class object">first class values</a>', so functions may be used as the inputs, or be returned as outputs from other functions. For example, the lambda term <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda x.x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/537ec33b43915b93dec1c98e433ec7a68bcab6a3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.049ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.x}"></span> represents the <a href="/wiki/Identity_function" title="Identity function">identity function</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x21A6;<!-- ↦ --></mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\mapsto x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/033c0ae81eaf4c65cbb0759d7aa2c4f434c00f02" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.273ex; height:1.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x\mapsto x}"></span>. Further, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda x.y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda x.y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/88b2e10a12e276198f384ca3f5da934bdfaedc07" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.874ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda x.y}"></span> represents the <i>constant function</i> <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x\mapsto y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x21A6;<!-- ↦ --></mo>
        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\mapsto y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/eb2452f2d32e5424f3db361de033fd49a73f9dcc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.099ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x\mapsto y}"></span>, the function that always returns <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle y}"></span>, no matter the input. As an example of a function operating on functions, the <a href="/wiki/Function_composition" title="Function composition">function composition</a> can be defined as <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda f.\lambda g.\lambda x.(f(gx))}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda f.\lambda g.\lambda x.(f(gx))}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/981d684cf4020a6c08224985d94a9d293b238fe6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.235ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \lambda f.\lambda g.\lambda x.(f(gx))}"></span>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Normal_forms_and_confluence">Normal forms and confluence</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Normal forms and confluence"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Normalization_property_(abstract_rewriting)" class="mw-redirect" title="Normalization property (abstract rewriting)">Normalization property (abstract rewriting)</a></div>
<p>It can be shown that β-reduction is <a href="/wiki/Confluence_(abstract_rewriting)" title="Confluence (abstract rewriting)">confluent</a> when working up to α-conversion (i.e. we consider two normal forms to be equal if it is possible to α-convert one into the other). If <a href="/wiki/Reduction_strategy_(lambda_calculus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Reduction strategy (lambda calculus)">repeated application</a> of the reduction steps eventually terminates, then by the <a href="/wiki/Church%E2%80%93Rosser_theorem" title="Church–Rosser theorem">Church–Rosser theorem</a> it will produce a unique <a href="/wiki/Beta_normal_form" title="Beta normal form">β-normal form</a>. However, the untyped lambda calculus as a <a href="/wiki/Rewrite_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Rewrite system">rewriting rule</a> under β-reduction is neither <a href="/wiki/Strongly_normalising" class="mw-redirect" title="Strongly normalising">strongly normalising</a> nor <a href="/wiki/Weakly_normalising" class="mw-redirect" title="Weakly normalising">weakly normalising</a>; there are terms with no normal form such as <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886049734">.mw-parser-output .monospaced{font-family:monospace,monospace}</style><span class="monospaced"><b>Ω</b></span>.
</p><p>Considering individual terms, both strongly normalising terms and weakly normalising terms have a unique normal form. For strongly normalising terms, any reduction strategy is guaranteed to yield the normal form, whereas for weakly normalising terms, some reduction strategies may fail to find it.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Encoding_datatypes">Encoding datatypes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Encoding datatypes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Church_encoding" title="Church encoding">Church encoding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mogensen%E2%80%93Scott_encoding" title="Mogensen–Scott encoding">Mogensen–Scott encoding</a></div>
<p>The basic lambda calculus may be used to model <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic" title="Arithmetic">arithmetic</a>, Booleans, data structures, and recursion, as illustrated in the following sub-sections <i><a href="#Arithmetic_in_lambda_calculus">i</a></i>, <i><a href="#Logic_and_predicates">ii</a></i>, <i><a href="#Pairs">iii</a></i>, and <i><a href="#Recursion_and_fixed_points">§ iv</a></i>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Arithmetic_in_lambda_calculus">Arithmetic in lambda calculus</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Arithmetic in lambda calculus"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There are several possible ways to define the <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a> in lambda calculus, but by far the most common are the <a href="/wiki/Church_numeral" class="mw-redirect" title="Church numeral">Church numerals</a>, which can be defined as follows:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">0&#160;:= λ<i>f</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>x</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">1&#160;:= λ<i>f</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>f</i> <i>x</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">2&#160;:= λ<i>f</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>f</i> (<i>f</i> <i>x</i>)</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">3&#160;:= λ<i>f</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>f</i> (<i>f</i> (<i>f</i> <i>x</i>))</span></dd></dl>
<p>and so on. Or using an alternative syntax allowing multiple uncurried arguments to a function:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">0&#160;:= λ<i>fx</i>.<i>x</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">1&#160;:= λ<i>fx</i>.<i>f</i> <i>x</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">2&#160;:= λ<i>fx</i>.<i>f</i> (<i>f</i> <i>x</i>)</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">3&#160;:= λ<i>fx</i>.<i>f</i> (<i>f</i> (<i>f</i> <i>x</i>))</span></dd></dl>
<p>A Church numeral is a <a href="/wiki/Higher-order_function" title="Higher-order function">higher-order function</a>—it takes a single-argument function <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span>, and returns another single-argument function. The Church numeral <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> is a function that takes a function <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> as argument and returns the <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span>-th <a href="/wiki/Function_composition" title="Function composition">composition</a> of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span>, i.e. the function <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> composed with itself <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> times. This is denoted <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i><sup>(<i>n</i>)</sup></span> and is in fact the <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span>-th power of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> (considered as an operator); <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i><sup>(0)</sup></span> is defined to be the identity function. Functional composition is <a href="/wiki/Function_composition#Properties" title="Function composition">associative</a>, and so, such repeated compositions of a single function <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> obey two <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_exponents" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws of exponents">laws of exponents</a>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i><sup>(<i>m</i>)</sup>∘<i>f</i><sup>(<i>n</i>)</sup> = <i>f</i><sup>(<i>m+n</i>)</sup></span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<i>f</i><sup>(<i>n</i>)</sup>)<sup>(<i>m</i>)</sup> = <i>f</i><sup>(<i>m*n</i>)</sup></span>, which is why these numerals can be used for arithmetic. (In Church's original lambda calculus, the formal parameter of a lambda expression was required to occur at least once in the function body, which made the above definition of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">0</span> impossible.)
</p><p>One way of thinking about the Church numeral <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span>, which is often useful when analyzing programs, is as an instruction 'repeat <i>n</i> times'. For example, using the <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PAIR</span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NIL</span> functions defined below, one can define a function that constructs a (<a href="/wiki/Linked_list" title="Linked list">linked</a>) <a href="/wiki/Cons#Lists" title="Cons">list</a> of <i>n</i> elements all equal to <i>x</i> by repeating 'prepend another <i>x</i> element' <i>n</i> times, starting from an empty list. The lambda term 
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">λ<i>n</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>n</i> (PAIR <i>x</i>) NIL</span></dd></dl>
<p>creates, given a Church numeral <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> and some <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>x</i></span>, a sequence of <i>n</i> applications
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PAIR <i>x</i> (PAIR <i>x</i>...(PAIR <i>x</i> NIL)...)</span></dd></dl>
<p>By varying what is being repeated, and what argument(s) that function being repeated is applied to, a great many different effects can be achieved.
</p><p>We can define a successor function, which takes a Church numeral <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> and returns its successor <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i> + 1</span> by performing one additional application of the function <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> it is supplied with, where <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<i>n f x</i>)</span> means "<i>n</i> applications of <i>f</i> starting from <i>x</i>":
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">SUCC&#160;:= λ<i>n</i>.λ<i>f</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>f</i> (<i>n</i> <i>f</i> <i>x</i>)</span></dd></dl>
<p>Because the <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i></span>-th composition of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> composed with the <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span>-th composition of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> gives the <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i>+<i>n</i></span>-th composition of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i><sup>(<i>m</i>)</sup>∘<i>f</i><sup>(<i>n</i>)</sup> = <i>f</i><sup>(<i>m+n</i>)</sup></span>, addition can be defined as 
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PLUS&#160;:= λ<i>m</i>.λ<i>n</i>.λ<i>f</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>m</i> <i>f</i> (<i>n</i> <i>f</i> <i>x</i>)</span></dd></dl>
<p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PLUS</span> can be thought of as a function taking two natural numbers as arguments and returning a natural number; it can be verified that
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PLUS 2 3</span></dd></dl>
<p>and
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">5</span></dd></dl>
<p>are beta-equivalent lambda expressions. Since adding <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i></span> to a number can be accomplished by repeating the successor operation <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i></span> times, an alternative definition is:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PLUS′&#160;:= λ<i>m</i>.λ<i>n</i>.<i>m</i> SUCC <i>n </i></span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Similarly, following <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<i>f</i><sup>(<i>n</i>)</sup>)<sup>(<i>m</i>)</sup> = <i>f</i><sup>(<i>m*n</i>)</sup></span>, multiplication can be defined as
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">MULT&#160;:= λ<i>m</i>.λ<i>n</i>.λ<i>f</i>.<i>m</i> (<i>n</i> <i>f</i>)</span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Selinger&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selinger-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Thus multiplication of Church numerals is simply their composition as functions. Alternatively
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">MULT′&#160;:= λ<i>m</i>.λ<i>n</i>.<i>m</i> (PLUS <i>n</i>) 0</span></dd></dl>
<p>since multiplying <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i></span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> is the same as adding <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> repeatedly, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i></span> times, starting from zero.
</p><p>Exponentiation, being the repeated multiplication of a number with itself, translates as a repeated composition of a Church numeral with itself, as a function. And repeated composition is what Church numerals <i>are</i>: 
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">POW&#160;:= λ<i>b</i>.λ<i>n</i>.<i>n</i> <i>b</i></span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-BarendregtBarendsen&#95;1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BarendregtBarendsen-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Alternatively here as well,
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">POW′&#160;:= λ<i>b</i>.λ<i>n</i>.<i>n</i> (MULT <i>b</i>) 1</span></dd></dl>
<p>Simplifying, it becomes
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">POW′′&#160;:= λ<i>b</i>.λ<i>n</i>.λ<i>f</i>.<i>n</i> <i>b</i> <i>f</i></span></dd></dl>
<p>but that is just an eta-expanded version of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">POW</span> we already have, above.
</p><p>The <i>predecessor</i> function, specified by two equations <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PRED (SUCC <i>n</i>) = <i>n</i></span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PRED 0 = 0</span>, is considerably more involved. The formula
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PRED&#160;:= λ<i>n</i>.λ<i>f</i>.λ<i>x</i>.<i>n</i> (λ<i>g</i>.λ<i>h</i>.<i>h</i> (<i>g</i> <i>f</i>)) (λ<i>u</i>.<i>x</i>) (λ<i>u</i>.<i>u</i>)</span></dd></dl>
<p>can be validated by showing inductively that if <i>T</i> denotes <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(λ<i>g</i>.λ<i>h</i>.<i>h</i> (<i>g</i> <i>f</i>))</span>, then <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">T<sup>(<i>n</i>)</sup>(λ<i>u</i>.<i>x</i>) = (λ<i>h</i>.<i>h</i>(<i>f</i><sup>(<i>n</i>−1)</sup>(<i>x</i>)))</span> for <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i> &gt; 0</span>. Two other definitions of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PRED</span> are given below, one using <a href="#Logic_and_predicates">conditionals</a> and the other using <a href="#Pairs">pairs</a>. With the predecessor function, subtraction is straightforward. Defining
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">SUB&#160;:= λ<i>m</i>.λ<i>n</i>.<i>n</i> PRED <i>m</i></span>,</dd></dl>
<p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">SUB <i>m</i> <i>n</i></span> yields <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i> − <i>n</i></span> when <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i> &gt; <i>n</i></span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">0</span> otherwise.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Logic_and_predicates">Logic and predicates</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Logic and predicates"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>By convention, the following two definitions (known as Church Booleans) are used for the Boolean values <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">TRUE</span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FALSE</span>:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">TRUE&#160;:= λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.<i>x</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FALSE&#160;:= λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.<i>y</i></span></dd></dl>
<p>Then, with these two lambda terms, we can define some logic operators (these are just possible formulations; other expressions could be equally correct):<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">AND&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.λ<i>q</i>.<i>p</i> <i>q</i> <i>p</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">OR&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.λ<i>q</i>.<i>p</i> <i>p</i> <i>q</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NOT&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.<i>p</i> FALSE TRUE</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">IFTHENELSE&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.λ<i>a</i>.λ<i>b</i>.<i>p</i> <i>a</i> <i>b</i></span></dd></dl>
<p>We are now able to compute some logic functions, for example:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">AND TRUE FALSE</span>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">≡ (λ<i>p</i>.λ<i>q</i>.<i>p</i> <i>q</i> <i>p</i>) TRUE FALSE →<sub>β</sub> TRUE FALSE TRUE</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">≡ (λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.<i>x</i>) FALSE TRUE →<sub>β</sub> FALSE</span></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>and we see that <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">AND TRUE FALSE</span> is equivalent to <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FALSE</span>.
</p><p>A <i>predicate</i> is a function that returns a Boolean value. The most fundamental predicate is <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">ISZERO</span>, which returns <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">TRUE</span> if its argument is the Church numeral <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">0</span>, but <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FALSE</span> if its argument were any other Church numeral:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">ISZERO&#160;:= λ<i>n</i>.<i>n</i> (λ<i>x</i>.FALSE) TRUE</span></dd></dl>
<p>The following predicate tests whether the first argument is less-than-or-equal-to the second:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">LEQ&#160;:= λ<i>m</i>.λ<i>n</i>.ISZERO (SUB <i>m</i> <i>n</i>)</span>,</dd></dl>
<p>and since <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>m</i> = <i>n</i></span> if <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">LEQ <i>m</i> <i>n</i></span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">LEQ <i>n</i> <i>m</i></span>, it is straightforward to build a predicate for numerical equality.
</p><p>The availability of predicates and the above definition of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">TRUE</span> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FALSE</span> make it convenient to write "if-then-else" expressions in lambda calculus. For example, the predecessor function can be defined as:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PRED&#160;:= λ<i>n</i>.<i>n</i> (λ<i>g</i>.λ<i>k</i>.ISZERO (<i>g</i> 1) <i>k</i> (PLUS (<i>g</i> <i>k</i>) 1)) (λ<i>v</i>.0) 0</span></dd></dl>
<p>which can be verified by showing inductively that <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i> (λ<i>g</i>.λ<i>k</i>.ISZERO (<i>g</i> 1) <i>k</i> (PLUS (<i>g</i> <i>k</i>) 1)) (λ<i>v</i>.0)</span> is the add <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> − 1 function for <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>n</i></span> &gt; 0.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pairs">Pairs</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Pairs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A pair (2-tuple) encapsulates two values, and is represented by an abstraction that expects a handler to which it will pass the two values. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FIRST</span> returns the first element of the pair, and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">SECOND</span> returns the second.
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PAIR&#160;:= λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.λ<i>f</i>.<i>f</i> <i>x</i> <i>y</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FIRST&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.<i>p</i> (λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.<i>x</i>)</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">SECOND&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.<i>p</i> (λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.<i>y</i>)</span></dd></dl>
<p>A linked list can  either be NIL, representing the empty list, or a <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PAIR</span> of an element (so-called <i>head</i>) and a smaller list (<i>tail</i>). The predicate <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NULL</span> returns <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">TRUE</span> for the value <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NIL</span>, and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FALSE</span> for a non-empty list:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NIL&#160;:= λ<i>f</i>.TRUE</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NULL&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.<i>p</i> (λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.FALSE)</span></dd></dl>
<p>Alternatively, with <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NIL&#160;:= FALSE</span>, the construct <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<i>l</i> (λ<i>h</i>.λ<i>t</i>.λ<i>z</i>. ...<i>h</i>...<i>t</i>...) _on_nil_)</span> obviates the need for an explicit NULL test:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NIL&#160;:= λ<i>x</i>.λ<i>y</i>.<i>y</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">NULL&#160;:= λ<i>l</i>.<i>l</i> (λ<i>h</i>.λ<i>t</i>.λ<i>z</i>.FALSE) TRUE</span></dd></dl>
<p>As an example of the use of pairs, the shift-and-increment function that maps <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<i>m</i>, <i>n</i>)</span> to <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<i>n</i>, <i>n</i> + 1)</span> can be defined as
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">Φ&#160;:= λ<i>p</i>.PAIR (SECOND <i>p</i>) (SUCC (SECOND <i>p</i>))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">Ψ&#160;:= λ<i>fp</i>.PAIR (SECOND <i>p</i>) (f (SECOND <i>p</i>))</span></dd></dl>
<p>which  allows us to give perhaps the most transparent version of the predecessor function:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">PRED&#160;:= λ<i>n</i>.FIRST (<i>n</i> (Ψ SUCC) (PAIR 0 0))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">&#160; = λ<i>nfx</i>.FIRST (<i>n</i> (Ψ <i>f</i>) (PAIR <i>x x</i>))</span></dd></dl>
<p>Substituting the definitions and simplifying the resulting expression leads to streamlined definitions
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">&#160; = λ<i>nfx</i>.<i>n</i> (λ<i>rab</i>.<i>rb</i>(<i>fb</i>)) (λ<i>ab</i>.<i>a</i>) <i>x x</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">&#160; = λ<i>nfx</i>.<i>n</i> (λ<i>rij</i>.<i>j</i>(<i>rjf</i>)) (λ<i>ij</i>.<i>x</i>) I I</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">&#160; = λ<i>nfx</i>.<i>n</i> (λ<i>rij</i>.<i>i</i>(<i>rjj</i>)) (λ<i>ij</i>.<i>x</i>) I <i>f</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">&#160; = λ<i>nfx</i>.<i>n</i> (λ<i>ri</i>.<i>i</i>(<i>rf</i>)) (λ<i>i</i>.<i>x</i>) I</span></dd></dl>
<p>(where&#160; <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">I&#160;:= λ<i>x</i>.<i>x</i></span> ), evidently leading back to the original.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Additional_programming_techniques">Additional programming techniques</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Additional programming techniques"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There is a considerable body of <a href="/wiki/Programming_idiom" title="Programming idiom">programming idioms</a> for lambda calculus. Many of these were originally developed in the context of using lambda calculus as a foundation for <a href="/wiki/Semantics_(computer_science)" class="mw-redirect" title="Semantics (computer science)">programming language semantics</a>, effectively using lambda calculus as a <a href="/wiki/Low-level_programming_language" title="Low-level programming language">low-level programming language</a>. Because several programming languages include the lambda calculus (or something very similar) as a fragment, these techniques also see use in practical programming, but may then be perceived as obscure or foreign.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Named_constants">Named constants</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Named constants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In lambda calculus, a <a href="/wiki/Library_(computing)" title="Library (computing)">library</a> would take the form of a collection of previously defined functions, which as lambda-terms are merely particular constants. The pure lambda calculus does not have a concept of named constants since all atomic lambda-terms are variables, but one can emulate having named constants by setting aside a variable as the name of the constant, using abstraction to bind that variable in the main body, and apply that abstraction to the intended definition. Thus to use <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> to mean <i>N</i> (some explicit lambda-term) in <i>M</i> (another lambda-term, the "main program"), one can say
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(λ<i>f</i>.</span><i>M</i><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">)</span> <i>N</i></dd></dl>
<p>Authors often introduce <a href="/wiki/Syntactic_sugar" title="Syntactic sugar">syntactic sugar</a>, such as <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">let</span>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>e<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to permit writing the above in the more intuitive order
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">let <i>f</i> =</span> <i>N</i> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">in</span> <i>M</i></dd></dl>
<p>By chaining such definitions, one can write a lambda calculus "program" as zero or more function definitions, followed by one lambda-term using those functions that constitutes the main body of the program.
</p><p>A notable restriction of this <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">let</span> is that the name <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> may not be referenced in <i>N</i>, for <i>N</i> is outside the scope of the abstraction binding <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span>, which is <i>M</i>; this means a recursive function definition cannot be written with <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">let</span>. The <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">letrec</span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ariola&#95;29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ariola-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>f<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> construction would allow writing recursive function definitions, where the scope of the abstraction binding <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>f</i></span> includes <i>N</i> as well as <i>M</i>. Or self-application a-la that which leads to <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><b>Y</b></span> combinator could be used.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Recursion_and_fixed_points">Recursion and fixed points</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lambda_calculus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Recursion and fixed points"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Fixed-point_combinator" title="Fixed-point combinator">Fixed-point combinator</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/SKI_combinator_calculus#Self-application_and_recursion" title="SKI combinator calculus">SKI combinator calculus §&#160;Self-application and recursion</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Recursion" title="Recursion">Recursion</a> is when a function invokes itself. What would a value be which were to represent such a function? It has to refer to itself somehow inside itself, just as the definition refers to itself inside itself. If this value were to contain itself by value, it would have to be of infinite size, which is impossible. Other notations, which support recursion natively, overcome this by referring to the function <i>by name</i> inside its definition. Lambda calculus cannot express this, since in it there simply are no names for terms to begin with, only arguments' names, i.e. parameters in abstractions. Thus, a lambda expression can receive itself as its argument and refer to (a copy of) itself via the corresponding parameter's name. This will work fine in case it was indeed called with itself as an argument. For example,  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(λ<i>x</i>.<i>x</i> <i>x</i>) <i>E</i> = (<i>E E</i>)</span> will express recursion when <i>E</i> is an abstraction which is applying its parameter to itself inside its body to express a recursive call. Since this parameter receives <i>E</i> as its value, its self-application will be the same <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<i>E E</i>)</span> again.
</p><p>As a concrete example, consider the <a href="/wiki/Factorial" title="Factorial">factorial</a> function <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">F(<i>n</i>)</span>, recursively defined by
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">F(<i>n</i>) = 1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × F(<i>n</i> − 1)</span>.</dd></dl>
<p>In the lambda expression which is to represent this function, a <i>parameter</i> (typically the first one) will be assumed to receive the lambda expression itself as its value, so that calling it with itself as its first argument will amount to the recursive call. Thus to achieve recursion, the intended-as-self-referencing argument (called <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>s</i></span> here, reminiscent of "self", or "self-applying") must always be passed to itself within the function body at a recursive call point:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">E&#160;:= λ<i>s</i>. λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × (<i>s</i> <i>s</i> (<i>n</i>−1)))</span>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>with  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>s s n</i> = F <i>n</i> = E E <i>n</i></span>  to hold, so  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>s</i> = E</span>  and</dd></dl></dd></dl></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">F&#160;:= (λ<i>x</i>.<i>x</i> <i>x</i>) E = E E</span></dd></dl>
<p>and we have
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">F = E E = λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × (E E (<i>n</i>−1)))</span></dd></dl>
<p>Here <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>s s</i></span> becomes <i>the same</i> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"> (E E)</span> inside the result of the application <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"> (E E)</span>, and using the same function for a call is the definition of what recursion is. The self-application achieves replication here, passing the function's lambda expression on to the next invocation as an argument value, making it available to be referenced there by the parameter name <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>s</i></span> to be called via the self-application <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>s</i> <i>s</i></span>, again and again as needed, each time <i>re-creating</i> the lambda-term <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"> F = E E</span>. 
</p><p>The application is an additional step just as the name lookup would be. It has the same delaying effect. Instead of having <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"> F</span> inside itself as a whole <i>up-front</i>, delaying its re-creation until the next call makes its existence possible by having two <i>finite</i> lambda-terms <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"> E</span> inside it re-create it on the fly <i>later</i> as needed.
</p><p>This self-applicational approach solves it, but requires re-writing each recursive call as a self-application. We would like to have a generic solution, without the need for any re-writes:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">G&#160;:= λ<i>r</i>. λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × (<i>r</i> (<i>n</i>−1)))</span>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>with  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>r</i> <i>x</i> = F <i>x</i> = G <i>r</i> <i>x</i></span>  to hold, so  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>r</i> = G <i>r</i> =: FIX G</span>  and</dd></dl></dd></dl></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">F&#160;:= FIX G</span>  where  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FIX <i>g</i> = (<i>r</i> where <i>r</i> = <i>g</i> <i>r</i>) = <i>g</i> (FIX <i>g</i>)</span>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>so that  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FIX G = G (FIX G) = (λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × ((FIX G) (<i>n</i>−1))))</span></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>Given a lambda term with first argument representing recursive call (e.g. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">G</span> here), the <i>fixed-point</i> combinator <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FIX</span> will return a self-replicating lambda expression representing the recursive function (here, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">F</span>). The function does not need to be explicitly passed to itself at any point, for the self-replication is arranged in advance, when it is created, to be done each time it is called. Thus the original lambda expression <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(FIX G)</span> is re-created inside itself, at call-point, achieving <a href="/wiki/Self-reference" title="Self-reference">self-reference</a>.
</p><p>In fact, there are many possible definitions for this <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">FIX</span> operator, the simplest of them being:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="anchor" id="Y"></span> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><b>Y</b>&#160;:= λ<i>g</i>.(λ<i>x</i>.<i>g</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>)) (λ<i>x</i>.<i>g</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>))</span></dd></dl>
<p>In the lambda calculus, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><b>Y</b> <i>g</i></span>  is a fixed-point of <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><i>g</i></span>, as it expands to:
</p>
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><b>Y</b> <i>g</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; (λ<i>h</i>.(λ<i>x</i>.<i>h</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>)) (λ<i>x</i>.<i>h</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>))) <i>g</i></span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; (λ<i>x</i>.<i>g</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>)) (λ<i>x</i>.<i>g</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; <i>g</i> ((λ<i>x</i>.<i>g</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>)) (λ<i>x</i>.<i>g</i> (<i>x</i> <i>x</i>)))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">&lt;~ <i>g</i> (<b>Y</b> <i>g</i>)</span></dd></dl>
<p>Now, to perform the recursive call to the factorial function for an argument <i>n</i>, we would simply call <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<b>Y</b> G) <i>n</i></span>. Given <i>n</i> = 4, for example, this gives:
</p>
<div style="font-size:85%;">
<dl><dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">(<b>Y</b> G) 4</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; G (<b>Y</b> G) 4</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; (λ<i>r</i>.λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × (<i>r</i> (<i>n</i>−1)))) (<b>Y</b> G) 4</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; (λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × ((<b>Y</b> G) (<i>n</i>−1)))) 4</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 1, if 4 = 0; else 4 × ((<b>Y</b> G) (4−1))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (G (<b>Y</b> G) (4−1))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × ((λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × ((<b>Y</b> G) (<i>n</i>−1)))) (4−1))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (1, if 3 = 0; else 3 × ((<b>Y</b> G) (3−1)))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (G (<b>Y</b> G) (3−1)))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × ((λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × ((<b>Y</b> G) (<i>n</i>−1)))) (3−1)))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (1, if 2 = 0; else 2 × ((<b>Y</b> G) (2−1))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (2 × (G (<b>Y</b> G) (2−1))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (2 × ((λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × ((<b>Y</b> G) (<i>n</i>−1)))) (2−1))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (2 × (1, if 1 = 0; else 1 × ((<b>Y</b> G) (1−1)))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (2 × (1 × (G (<b>Y</b> G) (1−1)))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (2 × (1 × ((λ<i>n</i>.(1, if <i>n</i> = 0; else <i>n</i> × ((<b>Y</b> G) (<i>n</i>−1)))) (1−1)))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (2 × (1 × (1, if 0 = 0; else 0 × ((<b>Y</b> G) (0−1))))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 4 × (3 × (2 × (1 × (1))))</span></dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">~&gt; 24</span></dd></dl></div>
<p>Every recursively defined function can be seen as a fixed point of some suitably defined higher order function (also known as functional) closing over the recursive call with an extra argument. Therefore, using <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced"><b>Y</b></span>, every recursive function can be expressed as a lambda expression. In particular, we can now cleanly define the subtraction, multiplication, and comparison predicates of natural numbers, using recursion.
</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/Fixed-point_combinator" title="Fixed-point combinator">Y combinator</a> is coded directly in a <a href="/wiki/Strict_programming_language" title="Strict programming language">strict programming language</a>, the applicative order of evaluation used in such languages will cause an attempt to fully expand the internal self-application <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (xx)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (xx)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8594ad762fca4d2c9dc000b336046e3e2c1a66d1" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.469ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (xx)}"></span> prematurely, causing <a href="/wiki/Stack_overflow" title="Stack overflow">stack overflow</a> or, in case of <a href="/wiki/Tail_call_optimization" class="mw-redirect" title="Tail call optimization">tail call optimization</a>, indefinite looping.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A delayed variant of Y, the <a href="/wiki/Z_combinator" class="mw-redirect" title="Z combinator">Z combinator</a>, can be used in such languages. It has the internal self-application hidden behind an extra abstraction through <a href="#η-conversion">eta-expansion</a>, as <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (\lambda v.xxv)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>v</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mi>v</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (\lambda v.xxv)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d75086086461969e029258480b0c5cac4c084afc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.113ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (\lambda v.xxv)}"></span>, thus preventing its premature expansion:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle Z=\lambda f.(\lambda x.f(\lambda v.xxv))\ (\lambda x.f(\lambda v.xxv))\ .}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>Z</mi>

        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>v</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mi>v</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03BB;<!-- λ --></mi>
        <mi>x</mi>

        <mi>v</mi>
